A Small Chronicle of the World 118

— Haike

▲ In Hertfordshire, England's Audiford, there are more than 250 elderly people over the age of 75 who are still engaged in various jobs and do not stop working due to old age.

▲ In the early years of the European War, almost 1,000 French army cannons exploded due to incomplete fuses.

▲ The stroller, which is commonly seen in parks and streets, had its first one made in 1780 for the daughter of the fifth Duke of Deronshire in the world.

▲ Londoners are planning to travel to the Swiss Alps by plane and return to London on the same day.

▲ On the coast of Orkney Island, north of England, there is a seaweed that contains a chemical action. If it is combined with coal ash, it can be used as an excellent fuel.

▲ The British diamond polishing factory was opened in Brighton in 1917. It is the only one in the UK. After the end of the war, it accommodated 2,000 wounded soldiers into the factory to work.

▲ Although telegrams are also used in Uganda in central Africa, they are often blocked and inaccessible because the wires on the telephone poles are often cut off by workers to make bracelets, necklaces, and anklets.

The Death of a Drunken Beggar 119

— Zheng Yimei

It is a tragedy for literature when great figures pass away. After the deaths of Fan Shan Hanyun, we now hear of the passing of Zou Hanfei. Hanfei, a native of Liangxi, was uninhibited and loved to drink, hence the self-proclaimed title of "Drunken Beggar." He and other poets like Gao Taichi and Shu Wenmei formed the Xi Society, preserving and discussing old learning. The Drunken Beggar also excelled in parallel prose, his writings adorned with beautiful language. At times, he composed lyrics that were so captivating, filled with emotion, that they stirred the soul. I recall the celebration of Shu Wenmei's seventieth birthday held in a secluded temple outside Fengxi in Wu. Friends gathered to offer blessings, and I was among them. I heard that the Drunken Beggar had come all the way from Shanghai to congratulate him, and I admired him, hoping to deepen our acquaintance. Later, the Drunken Beggar arrived by rickshaw from Jinchang, directly to Fengxi. However, the rickshaw overturned halfway, and the Drunken Beggar injured his leg, causing severe pain. Wenmei, feeling apologetic, sent him to a nearby hospital for treatment. He groaned for several days before recovering, but his gait was stiff, as the tendons and bones were damaged beyond repair. The Drunken Beggar then said with a smile, "From now on, the Drunken Beggar should be renamed the Lame Beggar." He lived in Xujiahui, Shanghai, and due to old age and a bad leg, he named his residence "Waiting for Death Tower" and wrote "Waiting for Death Tower Record," which was widely circulated. However, living in Shanghai was difficult, so he had to return to his hometown and reside in the library, living on a meager salary. He died in poverty and hardship. It is a pity that he had many writings, mostly scattered in newspapers and the Xi Society journal. Last winter, his disciples and old friends raised funds to carve his works, but before they could be completed, he passed away. The death of the Drunken Beggar is deeply regrettable.

By the Shores of Tai Lake 120

— Fen Lü

The day after my visit to Suzhou, I traveled with my companions Ping and Geng to Liangxi to visit many, arriving late at the foot of Wenxi Building. I then went to Plum Garden. Revisit this place, the changes in my life are as if in a dream. The flowing water beneath Sky Heart Terrace remains, and the ten thousand fragrant plum trees still bloom profusely. In the clear scenery, there is no one walking on the short fences and winding paths. I feel as if I have entered a painting. From Fragrant Snow Sea to Reciting Bin Hall, plum trees are planted everywhere, but Little Luofu is the best. The fine grass there is like a carpet. I lay down on the ground, thinking of the setting moon. Truly, I do not know what age it is. Beside Tai Lake, a newly built hotel is full of picturesque and poetic intent. It's a pity that the railings are unable to accommodate me leaning against them, so I skirt around Zongjing Villa. From the terrace, the distant trees fill my eyes, so vast. This is the best spot in the whole garden. Below the terrace, there is the sound of reading. A famous garden with scholarly recitation is a rare blessing in life. Now, people are sad about the past. After leaving Plum Garden, I walked about four miles to Little Ji Mountain. The mountain is by Tai Lake, facing Wanjing Hall and Yuantouzhu across the water. Tea sellers wave flags, inviting people to cross. Drifting along, I feel like a grain of rice in the vast world. After twenty minutes by boat, I reached Yuantouzhu. The magnificent pavilions and high buildings form a famous scenic area. The mountain is not very high, but the climate is refreshing and suitable for a secluded residence. Reading and painting, the sound of the waves enters the lake tower. The morning and evening light embraces one’s heart. Such rare pleasures are hard to find in the world. I then think of the warm thoughts that arise in the hearts of dusty, worldly people. For me, the mountains and rivers are truly delicious, even better than the first time I came. Circling around the mountain, I gradually entered a space of short pine trees and broken rocks. I heard people's voices, faintly indistinguishable. I finally saw workers carving stones, starting to build gardens anew. From here to Treasure Box, I knew it was not far. I planned to explore further, but my companions were lagging behind, and my strength was failing, so I returned. I found Lü Ping by the lake, sitting on a thin rock, leaning against a lone pine tree. The mountains and lakes remain unchanged since the last time I traveled here. When I reached Guangfu Temple and heard the sutras, I tried tea at Flying Cloud Pavilion. The cliff carvings of "Containing Wu and Yue" and the characters of "Horizontal Clouds" are still there. The waves on the lake and the setting sun have gathered the boats, and laughter is gradually diminishing. I made a dream of the empty mountain and waited for the ferry. When I returned by boat, I felt that this trip was not easy to obtain.

Omen in a Signature 121

— Fei Wenbao

Mr. Yuan Hanyun from Huanshang is known in Jilin for his calligraphy and writings. When corresponding with friends, he always signed with the three characters "Wen Dun Shou" (文頓首, "Respectfully bowing at the end"). His cursive writing was often connected like the number "二百" (two hundred). In his small works, he often signed "Hanyun" in the style of the "Seventeen Post Letter" (十七帖), resembling the name of Mr. Zhang Si from Nantong. He also often signed a single "Yun" (雲, "cloud") character in various forms, resembling the numbers "四二" (forty-two) or the character "了" (liao, "end"). Unfortunately, he suddenly passed away on the twenty-third of this month at the age of forty-two. In the past, people referred to death as "了" (liao, "end"). Hanyun's signature had already foreshadowed the year of his death. Alas! (Que Chou)

A Record of the Robot in the German Hygiene Museum 122

— Xu Shiqi

During the spring, I was dispatched by the Health Department of the League of Nations in Geneva to the German Hygiene Museum in Dresden to study the creation of medical models and the content equipment. After observing and studying, I would like to introduce to the countrymen what I saw.

Germany has always been known for its medical science. The innovation everywhere can show the spirit of science. Since 1911, the International Hygiene Exhibition has been held in Dresden to exchange medical knowledge internationally to promote public health. It was not able to continue because of the impact of the European War. Now it has been twenty years. Last summer, the Hygiene Exhibition was reopened. Twenty-four countries participated, covering an area of 400,000 square meters. At the same time, the great and profound Hygiene Museum was completed and officially established, becoming a unique feature in the world of medicine.

Among the most refined exhibits, there is only the robot Der durchsichting Kunstllche Mensch. The whole body is transparent, and all kinds of organs are equipped, which is extremely complex. It is placed in the central hall in a standing position with its head raised and hands outstretched. The internal device is equipped with electric lights and key activation. The brain of the robot glows vividly and is released simultaneously with text descriptions for about one or two minutes. Then, in turn, the audience can see clearly at a glance, which is extremely valuable in public health publicity. It is heard that the research and manufacture of the robot took ten years, and it took the efforts of dozens of medical scientists and technicians to complete it.

My country's science and medical skills are just beginning to sprout, and the voices of preserving old medicine are loud. People in the community often blame the inferior skills of doctors for the inadequacy of science and medicine. Will ignoring food because of choking be a chance to promote science? Looking at the creations and inventions of other countries, which are changing with each passing day, we should be more alert and work hard.

A Second Visit to See Paintings in Linggu 123

— Pengzhou

I visited the capital before and wrote "Visiting Linggu for Paintings," published in this newspaper for more than eight months. Now, I revisited Linggu with Yueqiu and others and met Mr. Liang Dingming in his newly built painting studio. At that time, Mr. Liang was painting two oil paintings for the National Government. They were both more than ten feet tall and wide, one being a portrait of Chairman Chiang in military uniform riding a horse, and the other being a scene of Mr. Chen Yingshi in prison.

Mr. Liang showed me a wooden model of a dedicated gallery for the memorial hall of martyred soldiers. The room was rectangular with slightly rounded ends. The roof was illuminated by a light. At both ends of the room, a high platform was built slightly away from the wall for easy viewing. The size of the murals was very large, and it was not appropriate to view them up close. The theme of the paintings was revolutionary battles, each taking a fierce and important scene as a representative. The battles approved by Chairman Chiang include the Mianhu Battle, the Huizhou Battle, the Dingsiqiao Battle, the Nanchang Battle, the Xuzhou Battle, the Jinan Battle, and the Jining Battle. In addition, Mr. Liang plans to make two more paintings, the Guide Battle and the Lanfeng Battle. Because the canvas order has not arrived, he has collected a lot of factual materials from the battles and has already drawn many drafts.

Mr. Liang also had an invention in this large mural project, namely a perspective line device. Because he suffered from inaccurate perspective lines when creating large murals, he invented this device, which has been quite successful. He used a small light bulb, suspending a black line horizontally in front of it, and placing a wooden board with black lines drawn on it below it. When the shadow of this horizontal black line coincides with the lines drawn on the wooden board, one end is displayed on the canvas. Mr. Liang said that this method is very convenient. After his large mural is completed, he will offer this new tool for perspective drawing to society. It is a pity that we did not get to test it at night.

Housing Shortage in the Capital 124

— Manyin

Everyone knows about the recent housing shortage in the capital. The root cause is the sharp increase in population, leading to an oversupply of housing demand. According to the population report investigated by the Capital Police Department, the population is more than 580,000, and the monthly statistics show that there is no decrease, but at least an increase of two or three thousand people per month. The old-fashioned houses in Nanjing are too unsuitable, and those that are slightly livable are very expensive. The rent is second only to Shanghai, and the labor and materials are rough and the buildings are inferior. In addition to the rent, a deposit is also required. The deposit is ten times the rent. If the deposit is three months' rent, it is still considered a lenient treatment for tenants. However, some people think that there is a lot of land in Nanjing. Why not engage in construction that benefits others and oneself? Why is the decision not made because there are few houses and many people? This is a mystery of the urban housing shortage. There is indeed a reason for this: landowners buy land and are lazy to engage in construction. The price of land in Nanjing has been rising day by day. Because of the housing shortage, the land price has increased even more. Therefore, landowners have a property that they bought last year, and they can sell it this year for double the profit, or they can wait until the second half of the year and the price will skyrocket. Why bother to work hard on construction, or suffer losses if they are not specialized in construction? In this way, they can profit from others' interests. The landowners all have this kind of thinking. Like the land in Shanghai, there is no need to produce all day long, and the land price is skyrocketing. A large piece of open space in Pingmen, Suzhou, was purchased by the Bei family, and there is still no construction to this day, but the land price has increased several times compared to when it was purchased. This is a kind of inert business method that is really unfair. Therefore, some people have proposed to imitate the Paris method in France, where the government buys a number of bases and builds medium-sized houses, dividing them into people and paying installments on time. This is enough to help alleviate the housing shortage.

Travels in India (XIII) 125

— Linghua

I got a treasure in the plantation, that is, the most famous bodhi tree. I only took two leaves, which said that there were bodhi trees everywhere in the countryside, but not many in the city. This tree is slightly like the banyan tree in Fujian and Guangdong, and the leaves are not very large, slightly like mulberry leaves, three inches in size and triangular in shape. It is heard that there are many bodhi trees in Bodh Gaya. I should return with a full load when I arrive there. The Bodhi tree Bodhi tree is also called the Ficus religiosa. The tree is mostly shaded, which can be an acre in size, and the circumference can be several meters. It is like the banyan tree in the south. The name Bodhi tree is because the Buddha sat under the tree and attained enlightenment. In fact, the Buddha is no different from all living beings. The Buddha tree is the tree for all living beings. The Bodhi tree is especially important in the Zen school, that is, the difference between the Southern School's Sixth Patriarch Huineng and the Northern School's Senior Monk Shenxiu's efforts and methods of enlightenment. The Sixth Patriarch's Platform Sutra details Shenxiu's verse: "The body is the bodhi tree," and the Sixth Ancestor's verse: "Bodhi is originally not a tree," using Prajna to break the emptiness to counteract it. Even "Dream of the Red Chamber" takes it to help the material of the beauty's Zen. It can be seen that the Bodhi tree is a major case in our ideological world. I am asking Indian friends for bodhi tree seeds to spread them widely in China, but it is also limited to the south. It is definitely impossible to transplant them to the north, because trees like bananas and banyans are almost all produced in the tropics. However, in every garden, they can be planted in greenhouses, that is, they can be cultivated as flowers and plants, and they can also be used as a great memorial for someone in the garden with a bodhi tree.

The sun sets in the west, and Indian men and women take their children and wait for the boat back to Calcutta. I am also coming back, the moon shines on the Ganges with rippling light. I write a poem to record it:

The holy water of the Ganges bathes the heart, and the continuous spiritual source flows for thousands of years. I wish to spread the seeds of the bodhi tree, and the green clouds will be widely covered in all directions.

On December 1, Master Daojie came to the Mahayana Buddhist Association to talk with Secretary Xin Han. I will translate as follows: Ask how many kinds of languages are commonly used in India? Which is the most widely used? Answer: There are many kinds of Indian languages. The characters used in the Buddhist scriptures are roughly divided into two types: One type that is popular in China and Japan is Sanskrit, which comes from northern India. The second type that is popular in Sri Lanka, Myanmar, and Siam is Pali, which comes from Sri Lanka. All the countries where Pali is popular are Theravada Buddhism. However, these two types of characters have become ancient texts, and they are no longer used now. They are all translated into modern languages so that they can be understood. Now, the language commonly used in the Calcutta area is Bengali because it is in the Bengal province. However, the birthplace of the Buddha is not in the Bengal province, but in the present-day country of Nepal. Although this country is small, it is still independent and guarded by high mountains and soldiers. It is about 400 miles away from Calcutta, and it takes three days by train. Ask what kind of version of the Buddhist scriptures exists? Answer: The oldest ones are all written on palm tree leaves, so-called "beiye" (貝葉), which still exist today. Ask whether Myanmar has completely translated these palm leaf scriptures? Answer: It should have been translated completely. Xin Han asked whether there is Pali in China? I replied that I seemed to have never heard of a specialized school. Xin Han said that there is also a Pali department in Japan. I thought that Chinese Buddhists generally do not use scientific methods. The old and new are both broken. I once saw in the Buddhist Library established by Chinese Zeng Guangweng in the Leopard Rabbit area of Yangon that the catalog of English-Chinese Tripitaka translated by Japanese scholars was very detailed, and the names of each scripture have been translated completely, which is gratifying. There are also many English Buddhist books in the Penang Buddhist Society. In total, there are some more. Chinese Buddhism must go to Europe to learn. According to what I have seen in various places, there are already many English Buddhist books. The lack of academic talent and backwardness in everything is shameful.

Cotton Yarn: Dull Yarn Market 130

Yarn trading suspended for three days for the Spring Festival.

Yarn market prices fluctuated wildly, with losses in the morning and gains in the afternoon. Overseas cotton yarn conditions were trending downward, so most retail investors tended to short sell, and the pressure was still heavy. Currently, Qingdao buyers are purchasing yarn because most of the yarn factories there have switched to spinning fine yarn of 16 counts and are short of yarn, so they are purchasing from Shanghai. As a result, coarse yarn trading has picked up. The standard cotton yarn market will be closed for three days starting today for the Spring Festival, and business will resume as usual on the 7th. According to inquiries from Guangdong brokers, the Guangdong traders reported that the previous inventory in Guangdong was about 10,000 bales, and a considerable amount has been sold. Now there are still more than 10,000 bales. If these traders start early, they can expect a rebound by the end of this month. In fact, if the market can be developed, there is hope for a price increase.

The People's Standard started low in the morning and rebounded in the afternoon. The People's Standard market opened with lower prices in the morning due to the decline in American cotton, which softened market sentiment. The sellers were pressing down, and the market was very weak, with near-term prices falling by 49 qian and distant prices remaining flat. When the afternoon market opened, the market atmosphere was still scattered. At the close, it was heard that spot sales were active, and each price rose by 2, 3, or 4 qian. The total daily transaction volume was 12,300 bales. According to investigations, Shen Ji sold 650 bales, Rongxing sold 850 bales, and Yiyu sold 400 bales. Changfeng bought 950 bales, Gongtai bought 950 bales, and Tianlong bought 600 bales. The closing prices are recorded below.

Grains: Hankou Merchants Tentatively Purchase Jiangxi Rice 134

Yesterday, the late Indica rice market was weak. In the morning, only Shantou merchants offered to purchase one hundred bags of Jiangxi Zhongguan machine-milled rice at eleven yuan and eight jiao each. There were almost no transactions for late Indica rice. In the afternoon, as merchants felt there were no outlets for both domestic and foreign rice, some were willing to lower prices to sell off their stock. Hankou merchants, seeing that rice prices in their area were high, took the opportunity to tentatively purchase four hundred bags of late Jiangxi machine-milled rice at eleven yuan and one or two jiao each. Although the quality of the goods was slightly lower, the price was still two or three jiao higher than the previous month's market price. After this transaction, the market became slightly more active, and there is hope for a turnaround if there are continued outlets.

Flour Market Advances Sharply 135

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in both the morning and afternoon, prices for all months rose in unison. Recently, a certain factory has been buying to cover its short positions in foreign flour, and scattered merchants have also been purchasing, causing prices to rise even more sharply. With new bullish investors and scattered factories continuing to buy, the market became increasingly active. The April price rose to two liang and seven fen due to the demand for spot flour and purchases by a certain factory. Prices for other months also generally rose to two liang and four or five fen. The final closing price was higher than the previous day's closing price: July, up five fen; April, May, and June, up four and a half fen each; September, up three and three-quarters fen; July and August, up three and a half fen each.

Wheat Prices Gradually Rise 136

Yesterday, in both the morning and afternoon sessions of the wheat market, prices for both near-term and deferred contracts were on the rise. Deferred contracts rose because it was difficult to determine the price of foreign wheat, and speculators with insufficient capital had no choice but to lower prices to cover their positions. Near-term contracts did not rise as sharply as deferred contracts because a batch of foreign wheat was scheduled to arrive soon. However, both those selling on the float and new buyers purchased as much as possible, and prices rose steadily. The final closing price for September rose another nine fen, July rose eight fen, August rose seven fen, and April, May, and June each rose six fen.

Correction: Yesterday's report mentioned the registration of foreign wheat purchases. According to a letter from the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, how to handle this matter has not yet been decided, and the relevant industries are still being surveyed. The previous report was not factual, and we hereby issue a correction.

Record of the King of Siam's Visit to Shanghai Yesterday 140

Foreign Minister Wang and Mayor Zhang Boarded the Ship to Welcome Him

The King of Siam and Queen Tour the Huangpu River for Two Hours

King Prajadhipok of Siam, accompanied by Queen Rambai Barni and his uncle Prince Svasti, along with a party of fourteen, arrived in Shanghai at 11:30 yesterday morning aboard the Japanese Empress liner. They toured the Huangpu River for two hours without disembarking. This morning at nine o'clock, they will depart on the same ship to travel east.

Grand Welcome: As the Japanese Empress steamed into the Wusongkou, Chinese warships fired salute cannons in respect. Shortly after, the ship docked at the Jardine Matheson Wharf in Pudong. The Chinese flag and the Siamese flag were raised high, fluttering in the wind. The Songhu Garrison Headquarters dispatched a company of infantry, and the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau sent a company of police to stand guard. As the Siamese King's ship docked, they all fired their guns in salute. The Siamese King and Queen were on the deck, admiring the sights of Shanghai and taking pictures with a camera. First, Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, representing National Government Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, and Shanghai Mayor Zhang Qun, representing Songhu Garrison Commander Xiong Shihui, along with Hu Shize, Director of the Asian Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Secretary Liu Yunfang, Section Chief Bi Mingyu, and Shanghai Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, took a photograph when the Siamese King and Queen visited Shanghai. (Photographed by our newspaper)

Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, accompanied by the Siamese Ambassador to Japan, Sombat Pichai, boarded the customs patrol boat Jinhui at the new customs pier around twelve o'clock to welcome the guests on the Huangpu River. After boarding the Japanese Empress, Ambassador Sombat Pichai invited the welcoming officials to lunch on the ship.

Wang and Zhang Pay Respects: At three o'clock in the afternoon, Ambassador Sombat Pichai led Foreign Minister Wang and Mayor Zhang into the Siamese King's cabin, number 137, to pay their respects to the King and Queen. Foreign Minister Wang immediately inquired about the health of the King and Queen, and the King also inquired about the health of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. He also told Mayor Zhang that Shanghai was very developed. They talked for about ten minutes before leaving. Foreign Minister Wang and Mayor Zhang then spoke with Prince Svasti for another ten minutes in the living room. Foreign Minister Wang then instructed Secretary Liu to accompany Prince Svasti to Pudong to shop. Ambassador Sombat Pichai then presented Foreign Minister Wang with a photograph of the Siamese King and Queen to be given to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. At four o'clock, Foreign Minister Wang and Mayor Zhang, along with the welcoming officials, crossed the Huangpu River and returned. Director Hu remained to guide the Siamese King on a tour of the Huangpu River.

The Siamese King Tours the Huangpu River: At 4:20 p.m., the Siamese King, accompanied by the Queen and two attendants, left the Japanese Empress and boarded the Jinhui patrol boat to begin a tour of the Huangpu River. Director Hu and Ambassador Sombat Pichai accompanied them as guides. Customs water police dispatched another boat to guard behind them. The King was wearing a dark gray suit, was of small build, and had a short mustache on his upper lip. He spoke English fluently. The Queen wore a bright pink suit and had a radiant smile. The jade pendant given by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek was hung on her chest. The Jinhui patrol boat sailed up the Huangpu River. Warships and merchant ships in the river all flew flags in welcome. As the Siamese King's boat passed, sailors on Chinese and foreign warships took turns blowing their horns and firing their guns in salute. The Siamese King toured as far as the Gaochang Temple and the Jiangnan Shipyard before returning. He returned to the Japanese Empress at 6 p.m.

Prince Svasti's Remarks: Prince Svasti of Siam received a reporter from this newspaper on the Japanese Empress. He said that the King was thirty-five years old, had studied in England and France, and had studied artillery in England. He has been on the throne for five years and enjoys playing tennis and golf. Dancing is prohibited in the country because Siam follows Buddhism as the state religion and reveres the teachings of Confucius. Even now, men and women still do not touch each other when giving and receiving. The Queen is twenty-five years old. The King plans to stay in the United States for six months to treat an eye disease. He will return on the Japanese Empress by the same route, passing through Shanghai again. Prince Svasti himself is currently the Minister of Sanitation.

Departing This Morning on the Asama Maru

The National Government has appointed nine special commissioners to Japan for inspection: Xu Zonghao, Secretary of the Examination Yuan; Shen Xiding, Counselor; Shen Shiyuan, Secretary-General of the Examination Commission; Ma Honghuan, Secretary-General of the Ministry of Personnel; Li Danian, Counselor of the Executive Yuan; Hu Mai, Secretary; Huang Yuanduan, Counselor of the Ministry of Interior; Zhu Baoqin, Counselor of the Ministry of Education; and Xiong Hengfei, Section Chief of the Ministry of Industry. Chinese Children's Welfare Association Promotes Children's Day 142

Detailed Background

The Chinese Children's Welfare Association, since its founding by Minister Kong Yongzhi and others three years ago, has been dedicated to "promoting and safeguarding children's rights and seeking happiness for children through all possible means." It has been working diligently and has achieved remarkable results. It has been actively promoting initiatives to benefit children whenever possible. It is now advocating for April 4th as Children's Day and has already submitted a report to the Chairman of the National Government, who has instructed the Executive Yuan to inform all relevant parties. As April 4th approaches, the association's efforts in promoting Children's Day are detailed below for the benefit of readers and to encourage further promotion. (The following is a transcript of the association's original text)

(1) The Origin of Promoting Children's Day: In China, it is customary to drink Tusu wine on New Year's Eve, with children drinking first to ward off disease. On the Shangsi Festival, children's faces are washed with peach blossoms, said to preserve their youth. On the Dragon Boat Festival, colored silk threads are tied to children's arms, said to ward off disasters. Children are always given priority on festive occasions, especially in spring. This is because spring is the beginning of the year, and children are the beginning of life. Therefore, warding off misfortune for children at this time shows that their well-being is carefully considered. However, the formal establishment of a Children's Day has never been heard of. Since Ellen Key advocated for the 20th century to be the century of the child, the world's attention has been focused on children. As a Western scholar said, "World culture is determined by the footsteps of children." In addition to engaging in children's welfare work, countries around the world have established Children's Day. Britain celebrates on July 14th, the United States on May 1st, and Japan even divides it into Girls' Day on March 3rd and Boys' Day on May 5th, which are observed nationwide. In the United States, the National Children's Welfare Conference has been held at the White House three times in the twenty years since 1909, demonstrating the attention paid to children's happiness.

(2) The Process of Promoting Children's Day: On March 7th, the association submitted a request to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, stating, "We hereby request permission to hold Children's Day and request that it be forwarded to promote the event. The strength of a nation depends on its people, and the strength of its people depends on its children. Children are the future masters of the nation and the center of cultural transmission. Countries around the world pay attention to children's welfare work, and there are children's laws, children's courts, children's affairs bureaus, and other facilities. The Geneva International Alliance has also issued a formal declaration on the protection of children's rights, and the United States celebrates Children's Day on May 1st. Japan celebrates Girls' Day on March 3rd and Boys' Day on May 5th, which are observed nationwide. According to our country's imperial system, there are provisions for caring for children, and ancient sages have taught us to cherish the young, indicating that we are not neglecting children's welfare. However, the country has faced many disasters, and although the state has established education officials and local areas have kindergartens and nurseries, many people regard them as insignificant. At a time when national education is not widespread and compulsory education is not implemented, a significant gesture is needed to awaken the people. We propose to select a date as Children's Day and follow the example of neighboring countries by requesting the National Government to issue an order for the entire country to observe it. On that day, lectures will be held on various measures to protect children's rights, arousing public attention and instilling in everyone the idea of caring for children and taking responsibility for their well-being. This will enable children to understand their position and expand the scope of children's welfare, laying the foundation for a strong nation and a strong race. If approved, we request that April 4th be designated as Children's Day and that all relevant authorities be ordered to hold celebrations to promote the event. This is because the date falls in spring and coincides with Arbor Day. In terms of climate, it is the same in the north and south, and it complements the previous "3/3," "5/5," "7/7," "9/9," and current "10/10" festivals without conflict. As the association is responsible for children's welfare, we dare to offer our humble suggestions (omitted below)." On the 13th, the Social Affairs Bureau issued Approval No. 7586, stating, "The submitted report has been read and found to be insightful. In addition to approving the submission of the report to the Municipal Government and then to the National Government for approval, a joint meeting of representatives from the Public Security, Education, and Health Bureaus, as well as the Shanghai Charity Federation, will be convened at 3 p.m. on the 16th of this month to solicit opinions. At that time, the association is requested to send a responsible representative to attend the meeting and present their views. This is the approval," etc. In compliance with this order, the association prepared materials and drafted a general outline of measures (temporarily omitted). At the joint meeting of representatives from the Social Affairs Bureau and other representatives, it was said that the matter concerned the entire country and had already been submitted to the Municipal Government and then to the National Government for approval. It should be handled after the National Government issues a clear order. On the 21st, the Social Affairs Bureau issued an order stating, "For notification: The association's request to designate Children's Day has been submitted and approved. The Municipal Government's Instruction No. 9469 states, "The submitted report has been read and should be forwarded for review and approval. This is the order," etc. In compliance with this order, the association collected materials and awaited the National Government's clear order. On April 2nd, the Social Affairs Bureau issued Instruction No. 8447, stating, "For notification: The association's request to designate Children's Day has been submitted and approved. The Municipal Government's Instruction No. 7779 states that the National Government's Civil Service Office has sent a letter stating that the Chairman has issued an order to the Municipal Government to forward the report from the Chinese Children's Welfare Association requesting that April 4th be designated as Children's Day to the Executive Yuan for review and approval. This is the order," etc. In compliance with this order, since the National Government has issued an order to the Executive Yuan for notification, the name of Children's Day has been obtained. However, due to the short timeframe, it is not possible to hold celebrations. Only the details of this case will be published for general knowledge as a prelude to next year's April 4th and as a decoration for this year's April 4th.

(3) Enthusiastic Support for Children's Day: Since the association initiated the promotion of Children's Day, it has received letters from all parties expressing their unanimous support. (1) Xiong Bing San, Director of the Xiangshan Children's Welfare Institute in Beiping, wrote, "I strongly support your association's proposal to promote April 4th as Children's Day, but I am not sure if it is confirmed. Please telegraph to confirm so that we can prepare for the celebration." (2) The Youth Section of the Taiyuan Youth Association wrote from Shanxi, "Your association's goal of promoting Children's Day on April 4th to seek happiness for children is admirable. Please send us the methods and procedures so that we can organize it." (3) A letter from Nantong stated, "Please inform us of the outline for the Children's Day publicity and celebration so that we can hold it in our area," etc. Many letters have been received in Shanghai inquiring about the methods, indicating that many places are expressing sympathy and support. This shows that the enthusiasm of our people for children's welfare is increasing daily, and the scope of children's welfare is expanding daily, which can be said to be a matter of great importance for the children of the whole country.

Significance of the Chinese Children's Welfare Association's Promotion of Children's Day 143

Children! What a sweet, lovable term, full of all comfort and all hope! The future world belongs to the children of today. Although all our noble ideals cannot be realized at present, they will surely blossom into bright flowers in their brand-new paradise in the future. Then, all personal, social, national, and even global problems can be solved. From this, we can see that the problem of children is actually the key to all problems, the root of all problems. If the ancient Greek philosopher Archimedes was right in saying, "Give me the power and I can change the face of the world," then we can boldly say, "Give me the children and I can transform human life." Ellen Key was the first to reveal this message. Her famous saying, "The twentieth century is the century of the child," has been deeply engraved in the hearts of all people and has generated great power. In August 1925, the International Children's Welfare Association held its first international conference in Brussels, Belgium, with more than 700 representatives from 54 countries (including China) attending. Five principles for protecting children's rights were established and announced to all countries of the world for unified compliance. The Geneva International League of Nations, recognizing the importance of the issue of children, also established a Children's Protection Committee in May 1925 to focus on working for the happiness of children. Many governments have established "children's bureaus" to take charge of specific responsibilities. Numerous children's welfare organizations have been organized by the people of various countries. Children's laws, children's courts, children's research, children's literature, children's health, children's education, children's playgrounds, children's movie theaters, and children's libraries are all issues that thoughtful and insightful people are enthusiastically exploring and pondering today. In general,

The twentieth century will truly become the century of the child. The world of today will truly become the world of the child. In this tide of promoting children's happiness, there is a new system that is particularly noteworthy and deeply interesting to our country, and that is the so-called Children's Day. When this festival is held, people across the country concentrate their thoughts and enthusiastically explore children's welfare issues, and children in general receive a special welcome from adults on that day. They each hold their own small banquets, inviting their young friends, busy and happy. It is truly a new system full of poetry. When the United States held Children's Day on May 1st of last year, play days and public speeches were launched across the country. The American Children's Hygiene Association distributed hygiene slogans across the country and questioned mothers across the country on various issues. The New York City government took this opportunity to carry out a campaign to eradicate diphtheria and vaccinated one million children between the ages of nine months and ten years in the city that day to prevent diphtheria. Other cities and states also carried out the campaign with similar enthusiasm, but each had its own special issues and special focus. In addition to convening a White House conference to discuss children's happiness on that day, President Hoover also opened the White House all day, welcoming children from all over the country to tour freely and visit the President and First Lady. When they left, Mr. and Mrs. Hoover gave each child a bag of candy and a small book. When Britain held Children's Day on July 14th of last year, Lady Colville served as the National Chairman, and the Countess of Airlie and Lady Clementine served as Vice-Chairmen. Public speeches and infant health competitions were held in various places. Under the leadership of city mayors and county magistrates, people enthusiastically donated to support the national children's welfare cause. When it was held in London, the Mayor and Mayoress expressed special support. Slogans promoting children's happiness could be found everywhere on major streets in the city. Countless women wore badges and went to and fro in the crowds to raise money for children's welfare. The King and Queen personally visited the National Mother and Child Welfare Promotion Association and commended the association's work. In the evening, a play day was held with the Central Police Band playing music and speeches by Mrs. Lemon, Miss Spencer, Miss Dowie, and many other children singing, playing musical instruments, and dancing. It was quite a sight. Every year on March 3rd, Japan holds Girls' Day. On that day, girls across the country dress up in beautiful clothes and display dolls and toys at home, gather with young companions, and hold small banquets. After the banquet, they practice singing, playing games, and bowing. Every year on May 5th, Japan holds Boys' Day, which is simpler and more masculine than Girls' Day. On that day, people across the country eat rice cakes (covered with green leaves) to show that they do not forget this festival and to implicitly wish for health. Boys across the country traditionally hang the weapons and armor they usually play with in appropriate places, decorated with battle flags, and display rice wine and calamus below for offering. This symbolizes a spirit of courage and enterprise. At the same time, companions are gathered for a simple banquet for unrestrained laughter and talk. After the banquet, they enter the bathroom for a hot bath, with several calamus leaves placed in the water. The subtle warmth and fragrance surround the room, making people feel refreshed and happy. Alas, we have seen the grand occasion of other people's Children's Day. How can we not be very envious? Unfortunately, our childhood has passed in silence. It is our responsibility to prevent the next generation of citizens from having such regrets. The ancients once said, "The stones of other mountains can be used to polish jade, and the stones of other mountains can be used to correct mistakes." We should certainly learn from other people's shortcomings, but we should also imitate and learn from their strengths. Looking at the Children's Day system as a whole, (1) it can awaken the public's awareness of children's welfare, (2) it can increase children's happiness, and (3) it can give the country an opportunity to carry out a special spiritual training for the next generation of citizens. This is certainly worth imitating and learning from us. The association is an organization in our country that coordinates all aspects of children's happiness. Because we feel that the issue of Children's Day is a very important issue, we submitted a request to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau on March 7th of this year to be forwarded to the Shanghai Municipal Government and then to the National Government, requesting that April 4th be designated as China's Children's Day. We have already received a notice from the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau on April 2nd stating that the Chairman of the National Government has instructed the Executive Yuan to forward the order to the association. From now on, in our country's history, in addition to Labor Day and Women's Day, a Children's Day will be added, which can be said to be an unprecedented event. Although there is not enough time to hold large-scale celebrations this time, I believe that by this day next year, all the people of our country, from the Chairman and committee members to the common people, will be able to work together to promote this new system with rich significance in a planned and organized way. The impact on the future fortunes of our Chinese nation can be said to be very great, and there is no need to say more. Men and women adults across the country, please do not neglect this festival and fail to live up to this festival! Boys and girls children across the country, please enjoy this festival as much as possible and make full use of this festival! Brilliant flowers and full fruits all depend on people's cultivation and care. Please remember to hold a children's welfare movement and promote the Children's Day on April 4th every year, and do not delay this great festival! Twenty-four three

Japanese Fishing Boats Rampant in Our Territorial Waters 144

Fishing off Sheshan

Colliding with and Capsizing Our Fishing Boats

Japanese fishing boats previously sank our fishing boats in the waters off Dinghai, causing huge losses. Negotiations were initiated but have not yet been resolved. Recently, a large number of Japanese fishing boats have entered our territorial waters to fish wantonly, and have collided with and capsized our fishing boats. We are urgently reporting what we have heard as follows:

Colliding with and Capsizing Our Fishing Boats: Recently, the yellow croaker season has begun in the waters of eastern Zhejiang, and fishermen from eastern Zhejiang are launching their boats to fish. Most of them are fishing in the waters off Sheshan and the Langgang reefs. However, after our fishing boats set sail, a large fleet of Japanese fishing boats arrived and invaded our territorial waters, also to compete for fishing off Sheshan. Although there are many Chinese fishing boats, they are not as large as the Japanese boats. Seeing that our good rights are being taken away by the Japanese boats, we are unwilling to give up and go forward to compete. However, the Japanese boats wantonly rammed our fishing boats, and several fishing boats were sunk. Fortunately, the people who fell into the water were rescued by fellow fishermen. The waters of eastern Zhejiang have been carved into the sphere of influence of Japanese fishing boats.

Telegraphic Request to Send Warships to Intercept: After this tragedy occurred, the fishermen of eastern Zhejiang felt that their livelihood was about to be cut off and could not sit idly by while their national territorial waters were seized by foreigners. Therefore, all the fishermen jointly elected representatives Shi Renhang to telegraph to the Navy and Industry Departments, saying that recently Japanese fishing boats have again invaded our territorial waters and are densely distributed in the waters off Sheshan and Langgang reefs, using giant ships and large nets to fish exhaustively. There are only a limited number of fish in the world. If they do not enter there, they will enter here. Therefore, our fishing boats have almost no fish entering their nets from spring to winter, while Japanese fishing boats are rampant on the sea, hostilely provoking. As soon as our boats approach, they collide with them, causing both people and boats to sink. They also clap their hands and laugh, which is extremely inhuman. We urgently request the Navy Department to send multiple warships to drive the Japanese boats out of the country as soon as possible, so that the millions of fishermen in eastern Zhejiang can still be saved. Otherwise, their right to life will be lost and the livelihood of the fishermen will be cut off.

The French Marines Withdraw from Xujiahui 145

Since the autumn of the 13th year of the Republic of China, when the Father of the Catholic Church in Xujiahui Town, west of Shanghai, petitioned the French Consul-General to dispatch more than 30 French marines to be stationed in the vicinity of the Catholic Church, nearly seven years have passed. Because of illegal martial law that obstructed traffic, drunkenness and causing trouble, molesting women, and other illegal acts, the various groups in the town repeatedly petitioned the authorities to negotiate with the French Consul for their withdrawal, but this was never carried out. On September 21, 1929, a truck carrying French marines ran over and killed Zhang Qingbao from Changshu. On November 8 of the same year, the French marines beat and injured two local citizens, Ding Jiaxun and Wang Youhai, at Tianyao Bridge. The gentry and merchants of the town could no longer tolerate it and organized the Xujiahui All Circles Support Association. Chairman Zhu Shiqi, together with Chen Junyi, a standing committee member of the Municipal Party Department and the People's Training Association, demanded conditions from the French authorities such as punishing the perpetrators, compensation, apology, and withdrawal of troops. The Chinese Ratepayers Association of the French Concession negotiated on behalf of the Support Association and resolved the matter on November 23. Except for the issue of troop withdrawal, which was not within the scope of the case and would be negotiated separately, the French authorities fully recognized the other conditions of punishing the perpetrators, compensation, and apology. Now, Liu Yunfang, the head of the second branch of the sixth district of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, has ordered the Father of the Catholic Church to withdraw the troops within a time limit because the Catholic Church is located in the Chinese territory and the French marines are not allowed to cross the border and garrison, which is a loss of national sovereignty. At the same time, he has submitted a request to the Public Security Bureau to forward it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate seriously with the French Consul. It is said that the French marines have all been withdrawn by the day before yesterday.

China Merchants Bureau Sends a Letter Requesting a Halt to the Private Transfer of Sanxin 146

Because the Bureau Once Invested a Large Number of Shares

After the sale of the Sanxin Cotton Mill, the China Merchants Bureau believed that the bureau had previously invested a large number of shares in the mill, and it was illegal for the Sheng family's descendants to sell the property without permission. Therefore, it sent a special letter to the municipal government requesting that the buying and selling parties and the workers of the mill be ordered to prohibit private transfer. According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the original text of the letter is as follows (China Merchants Bureau's letter to the Municipal Government): We are writing to inform you that in recent days, various newspapers have repeatedly reported on the sale of the machinery of the Sanxin Cotton Mill by the Sheng brothers and the repeated mediation of labor disputes by your Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to stop the buyer from taking over. We were deeply surprised to read about the various processes. We learned that last year, your government, on the order of the National Government, thoroughly investigated the estate of Sheng Xuanhuai, a former official of the Qing Dynasty. You sent a letter to our bureau requesting that we conduct an investigation of the Sheng family's property. We submitted a detailed list in reply to your government, in which the Sanxin Cotton Mill was included. Our bureau therefore investigated the history of the mill in detail and discovered that the mill was not purely the private property of the Sheng family. Our bureau is actually the largest shareholder and has various relationships such as paying for the mill's foundation, purchasing boilers, and providing loans. Later, Sheng Xuanhuai renamed the mill, appropriating public property for private use. In the end, he even pretended to be a British merchant and registered in Hong Kong to escape domestic jurisdiction, relying on foreign forces to achieve his plan of encroachment and seizure. From the early years of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty to the 16th year of the Republic of China, our bureau was always managed and controlled by Sheng Xuanhuai and his descendants. No one dared to report such fraudulent events. As time went by, the actual facts of the mill's operation gradually became unknown to people. The Sheng family was able to safely regard it as private property. According to our bureau's records, the Sanxin Cotton Mill was actually the Weaving Bureau established in the eighth year of Guangxu, with a total capital of 400,000 taels. In the 17th year of Guangxu, our bureau invested 112,000 taels. In the 19th year of Guangxu, the bureau was destroyed by fire, and the boilers and machinery were mostly lost. Sheng Xuanhuai took this opportunity to reorganize and expand the mill, renaming it the Huasheng Textile Bureau and increasing the capital to 800,000 taels. Our bureau invested 320,000 taels. This share certificate of our bureau was kept by Sheng Xuanhuai and is recorded in a very reliable document. In addition, our bureau also allocated funds for the Weaving Bureau to fill the foundation (the current site of the Sanxin Mill) and purchase boilers. After the renaming to Huasheng, several tens of thousands of taels were borrowed. Although the name of the Huasheng Mill was changed again and again, the capital and property remained as a whole. Although it was registered with the Hong Kong government under the name of Sanxin with a declared capital of 1.5 million taels, the actual capital was still virtualized by the increase in the original capital of Huasheng on the land. It is exactly the same as the matter of our bureau's commercial management, from 2 million taels to 4 million taels to 8.4 million taels. The share certificates of our bureau in the mill have been concealed and held by the Sheng family's descendants, with no intention of returning them to our bureau. Our bureau has conclusive evidence for all the above points. Therefore, our bureau is definitely a shareholder of the Sanxin Cotton Mill and is also a creditor. It is absolutely clear that the Sheng family's descendants cannot sell the property without permission before all the rights of our bureau are legally resolved. Fortunately, the sale of the mill has not yet been completed, and your government is impartially reviewing the matter. We sincerely request that you order all parties involved in the buying and selling and the workers of the mill to absolutely prohibit private transfer until all the rights of our bureau have been effectively recovered. Otherwise, it will be considered invalid. We believe that your government values national navigation industry and will be happy to assist. We are writing to inform you of the relationship between our bureau and the Sanxin Cotton Mill and the reason for requesting the prohibition of transfer. Please investigate and handle accordingly. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Government, Mayor Zhang (China Merchants Bureau's letter to the Sanxin Cotton Mill Union): We are writing to inform you that we were shocked to read in the recent newspapers about the sale of the Sanxin Cotton Mill by the Sheng family. The Sanxin Cotton Mill was originally the Shanghai Machine Weaving Bureau. In the 17th year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty, our bureau allocated more than 100,000 taels of shares. Later, when it was renamed Huasheng, Sheng Xuanhuai, the former director of our bureau, allocated more than 300,000 taels of bureau funds to invest in new shares, and Sheng allocated bureau funds to purchase land and excavate and fill the mud along the river. However, because Sheng had been in charge of both our bureau and the Sanxin Mill for many years, he was able to use his position to engage in fraud and embezzlement, and privately held these shares without handing them over. Moreover, during the era of commercial management, the Sheng family's descendants were directly and indirectly in charge of bureau affairs, and these fraudulent events were concealed and not investigated. When the National Government sent personnel to take over our bureau, Zhao, the former general manager, mentioned the relationship between our bureau and the mill in a letter replying to the Municipal Government when the National Government was investigating Sheng's traitorous property. Now that our bureau has been taken over by the state, these property rights that were encroached upon by Sheng are waiting to be investigated and recovered. However, the Sheng brothers have no scruples and sell the mill's foundation privately, disregarding our bureau's property rights and ignoring the livelihood of thousands of workers. This is extremely inappropriate. Our bureau cannot abandon its sovereignty and navigation rights. In addition to sending a letter to the Municipal Government based on the previous case to declare that it should prohibit its free sale, we are now sending a letter to the person in charge of the mill to come to the bureau to handle the matter. We also know that your association has the same purpose of loving the industry and loving the navigation industry and strongly opposes the sale of the mill. We are sending you a formal letter on the relationship between our bureau and the mill and hope that you will oppose anyone freely transferring it before the property rights issues between our bureau and the mill have been properly resolved. We hope that you will take note. Sincerely, Cotton Spinning Industry Union of the Third Special District

Conflict Between Shipyard Workers and Tram Conductors Yesterday 147

Workers Went on Strike for One Hour

The case of the fight between the ticket sellers of the China Merchants Tram Company and the craftsmen of the Naval Aviation Office has not yet been completely resolved. Yesterday at 1:00 PM, Zhou Xiaoliu, a craftsman from the Naval Jiangnan Shipyard, had another conflict with a conductor from the Tram Company, resulting in a one-hour strike by all the workers of the shipyard. Chen, the director of the shipyard, Shao Kuan, agreed to the conditions requested by the workers before they resumed work. The details of the conflict are recorded as follows:

Cause of the Conflict: At about 1:00 PM yesterday, just as the shipyard workers were going to work, more than ten craftsmen from the Naval Jiangnan Shipyard's bench department, including Zhou Xiaoliu, were riding the No. 4 China Merchants Tram from the entrance of the South District Fire Brigade to work at Gaochang Temple. When the tram arrived near the South Railway Station, Zhang Luansheng, conductor No. 18 of the Tram Company, boarded the tram and checked the passes of the craftsmen. The passes of the shipyard workers were issued by the Tram Company in the spring of the 18th year of the Republic of China. After more than a year, all the stamps and photos were blurred and indistinguishable. The passes used to be exchanged every quarter according to the regulations. Last year, the Tram Company notified the shipyard that it was not necessary to exchange the old passes for the convenience of procedures, and that the old passes were still valid. Therefore, they have not been exchanged until now. The conductor said that Zhou's pass was blurred and that the steel stamp and photo did not match, and that it was a fake. The two sides spoke rudely and a quarrel arose. At the same time, Lin Honghai and other craftsmen from the shipyard were also riding this tram and saw this situation. They mediated from the middle, but it turned into a brawl. When the tram arrived at the last stop of Gaochang Temple, the two sides got off the tram and turned into a fierce fight. The situation was very tense, with fists and feet flying. As a result, He Changshui, the ticket seller of Tram No. 12, was injured in the face.

Craftsmen Detained: At about 1:00 PM yesterday, Cao Jinyang, police officer No. 335 of the first team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, happened to be at Gaochang Temple. He, together with Liu Guiting, patrol officer No. 41 of the first district's headquarters, took both sides to the Gaochang Temple sub-station. Zhou Xiaoliu's boarding pass was taken to the company by the conductor. When all the workers of the shipyard heard the news, they were very angry. The Tram Company forcibly took back the pass without following the procedures, which caused the dispute. All the workers requested that the authorities seriously negotiate and went on strike for one hour. They all crowded to the Gaochang Temple sub-station in the second district to request their release. Ye Baoqi, the battalion commander of the Naval Guard Battalion, personally went to the second district sub-station and explained the situation. Patrol Officer Gao immediately handed Lin over to Ye and took him back. He also sent soldiers to maintain order. The ticket seller No. 12 was personally sent to the company by Patrol Officer Niu of the second district.

Workers' Strike: After this incident occurred, the shipyard workers went on strike for one hour. More than a hundred workers went to the shipyard's union to demand three conditions: (1) Issue new tram passes in the shortest possible time. (2) Order the company to publish an apology in the newspaper for the insulted workers. (3) The time for exchanging passes in the future must not exceed one year. Zhu Xiangkui and Hong Fushun and other members of the union's standing committee led all the workers to visit Chen, the director of the shipyard, Shao Kuan, and asked for instructions. Chen agreed to all the conditions one by one and issued a notice first asking the workers to resume work. All the workers were satisfied and immediately resumed work.

Chen's Statement: After mediating this incident, Chen ordered Battalion Commander Ye Baoqi to go to the Tram Company and ask General Manager Lu to come to the shipyard within one hour to discuss a solution. At the same time, the Social Affairs Bureau also heard the news and sent Zhu Jintao, an official from the third section, to the scene of the incident to conduct a detailed investigation and report it for verification. It is said that Mayor Zhang will be appointed as the mediator in the end.

More Than 40 Silk Factories in Zhabei Resumed Work Yesterday 148

Wage Issues Awaiting Resolution

All Arrested Workers Completely Released

The female workers of all 40 silk factories in Zhabei, including Fuchangtai, demanded the restoration of their original wages. They did not report to the relevant authorities in advance and suddenly went on strike together one afternoon. The Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus believed that it was related to local peace and tranquility and immediately issued a notice and advised them to resume work first and wait for the higher authorities to review and handle it. They all entered the factory yesterday morning to resume work and the arrested workers have also been released. The situation yesterday is recorded as follows:

Yesterday's Situation: At 4:00 AM yesterday morning, the silk factories opened as usual. The various sub-stations and police stations of the fourth district of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and the entire armed police officers of the third brigade were all on duty and patrolling. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent Zhu Guilin to accompany the chiefs and patrol officers of the various districts to the factories to advise the workers to resume work. The union also sent directors Yuan Yunlong, Wu Suzhen, Yan Aizhu, Wu Xiubao, and other staff members such as Li Tonggai to the factories in groups to mobilize and guide them. At that time, all the female workers were waiting near the factory gates to watch. After repeated persuasion, the female workers of more than 50 silk factories in Tanjiabang, Taiyangqiao, and Tanzhiwan in Zhabei entered the factory to resume work at about 8:00 AM. However, the number of workers who went to work was less in several factories. Except for several factories such as Dalai and Tianlai, which were closed as usual, only the two factories of Ding Su and Mailun on Yutong Road were voluntarily closed by the factory owners. When work resumed at 12:30 PM, there were slight disturbances among the female workers of the factories such as Yuanyuan, Longji, Chunmao, Yongyuan on Changan Road, and Jinyuan on Meiyuan Road. After the authorities and the union sent personnel to explain separately, they all entered the factory to resume work immediately.

Number of Factories Resumed Work: The silk factories that have resumed work include Zhabei, Xinzha, Hujiu Da, Xie Xingchang, Wufeng, Xie Chang, Shunfeng Yong, Baisi Yi, Xie Feng, Hua Qingshun, Baisi Er, Heng Kang, Fuchangtai, Fumin, Ding Changshun, Heng Changxin, Yuanyuan, Longji, Chunmao, Yongyuan, Tailai, Qingfeng, Jinyuan, Ruifeng Yu, Fuchangrun, Yongan, Qichang, and other more than 30 factories. Dasheng, Shen Changchu, Xincheng, Jiusun, Hengda, Jiulun in Tanjiabang, and Fengtai and Yongchang in Taiyangqiao, a total of more than 40 factories.

Authorities' Notice: Pan Gongzhan, the director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, issued Notice No. 8571 yesterday morning, which was posted at the gates of various silk factories, saying: "For the purpose of issuing a notice, it has been found that the entire strike by female workers of 18 silk factories including Fuchangtai in the Zhabei district was not known to the Zhabei District Silk Reeling Industry Union beforehand. It can be seen that there are troublemakers instigating it. In addition to strictly investigating and handling it, this notice is hereby issued to all female workers of the various silk factories in the district, who must all comply with it, resume work immediately, and wait for verification and handling. Do not wait and see and mislead yourself. Sincerely."

Notice to All Factories: Huang Jinfan, a committee member of the Silk Factory Association stationed in the Zhabei district, notified the factories two days ago, saying: "We are writing to inform you that this labor unrest is unreasonable. Today, the factories are checking the number of workers who have come to work, and it is expected that some of them are not there because they are afraid. This is also the scene after the labor unrest in the past. Tomorrow, we hope that your factory will open as usual to ensure work. Sincerely."

Union's Statement: The Zhabei District Silk Reeling Industry Union issued a notice to the workers yesterday, saying: "Dear friends, you must resume work quickly and do not listen to rumors. You must listen to our advice. You must know that a strike is the most unfortunate thing. If you want to restore your wages, you must of course submit it to the higher authorities through the union to resolve it. Now our union is actively handling it, and there will of course be a satisfactory result in the future. Dear workers, do not be used by others and resume work quickly! Only after resuming work can there be a solution. Workers, wake up! Obey the union's orders and resume work quickly!"

Order from the Social Affairs Bureau: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau issued an order to the Silk Factory Association yesterday, saying: "For the purpose of issuing an order, it has been found that the labor dispute of the female workers of the silk factories such as Fuchangtai in the Zhabei district has been mediated by our bureau by sending personnel to work with the police officers of the Public Security Bureau. According to reports, the factories have gradually resumed work at about 8:00 AM this morning. However, when the workers of the four factories of Ding Kang, Bao Lun, etc. went to work, the factory owners claimed that the machines were damaged and refused to allow them to work. In reality, although there was some broken glass during yesterday's chaos, the machines were not damaged. Today, all the factories have resumed work, but the workers of the four factories are scattered outside. If there is another dispute, it will inevitably be impossible to control. This order is hereby issued to the association to quickly order the factory owners to start work immediately. When starting work, the police should be sent to maintain order and there is no need to worry too much. If the dispute is expanded due to delay, the factory will be held responsible. Sincerely."

Workers Released: After the female workers of the silk factories in the Zhabei district went on strike, Zhang Sanzi, a female worker aged 20 from Taizhou, who was arrested by the Tanjiabang police station the day before yesterday for instigating the strike, lived on Jinlu Road. Two people were arrested by the second branch of the fourth district: Lu Wengshi, a female worker aged 28 from Taizhou, who lived on Hanzhong Road and was a worker at the Jinyuan factory No. 190, and Zhao Huashi, a female worker aged 29 from Yancheng, who lived on Gonghe Road and was a worker at the Xiecheng factory. They were immediately sent to the fourth district headquarters that day. After Zhou, the district chief, interrogated them, they were temporarily detained. By last night, the female workers of the silk factories had all resumed work, and the three people had no other circumstances. They were ordered to sign a guarantee and released.

Guo Bingwen Took Office as Director of the Bureau of Industry and Commerce Yesterday 153

Guo Bingwen, the former member of the Industry and Commerce Committee, was appointed as the director of the Bureau of Industry and Commerce and ordered to prepare for the establishment of the International Trade Bureau. Guo had repeatedly resigned from the position of director of the Bureau of Industry and Commerce due to his recent appointment as a representative of the China Committee of the International Chamber of Commerce to attend the Washington Conference, but he complied with the order and prepared the organizational regulations and budget draft of the International Trade Bureau for the ministry's selection due to the importance of international trade to the national economy. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce, because the plan was under review, telegraphed and urged Guo to take office at the Bureau of Industry and Commerce immediately. Guo arrived at the bureau yesterday to take over the work. Zhao Jinqing sent personnel to hand over the work separately and introduced Guo to all the staff. Zhao said in his speech that Director Guo's knowledge and experience were well known to his colleagues and did not need to be introduced. He also had more than 30 years of friendship with him. He was deeply grateful to have him come to the bureau to take over. In the future, he would use his knowledge, experience, and spirit of sacrifice to strive to develop international trade, which would definitely make a considerable contribution to the national economy and people's livelihood. Guo then spoke, saying that he had been handling the China-America Association for the Promotion of Culture and Education and other national diplomacy affairs abroad in recent years. He represented the National Federation of Commerce to attend the International Chamber of Commerce Conference in The Hague last year, and he also went to Europe to inspect the post-war economic construction of various countries. He felt that China's international trade was backward compared to Europe and the United States, and its economic construction was even more so. He could not compete in the world business arena unless he actively struggled. This time, Minister Kong insisted on appointing him as the director of this bureau and ordered him to prepare for the establishment of the International Trade Bureau. He hoped that the national people should have the obligation to serve the public and did not dare to refuse. He reluctantly came to take the post. This bureau was reorganized from the Economic Discussion Office. The office was established in the 9th year of the Republic of China and has achieved great results. The National Government established the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and sent personnel to take over the group as this bureau to collect and publicize domestic and foreign industrial and commercial news for the reference of entrepreneurs and to promote international trade. The task was extremely important. Under the guidance of Minister Kong, Director Zhao and his colleagues have made considerable progress in the past three years. Now that Director Zhao has been transferred to the ministry to take on an important position, the minister ordered him to come and take over. In the future, he will certainly follow the administrative plan of the ministry and carry it out practically. The colleagues are well versed in industrial and commercial enterprises and international economic issues. If they have any opinions, they are welcome to inform him at any time and jointly plan improvements, so that the original business can be operated in the most economical way and achieve the most magnificent efficiency. As for the issue of developing international trade, he also hopes that the colleagues will conduct practical research and give more guidance, so that he can make a contribution to the government and society.
