Fei Wenyuan Silver Shop Robbed in Broad Daylight 155

Five Robbers Visited the Silver Shop

Bought a Gold Thread Ring and Jumped into the Counter

Innocent Customers Suffered

Total Loss of Nearly 6,000 Yuan

Fei Wenyuan Silver Shop, in the prosperous area of Nanjing Road, was suddenly visited by five robbers in broad daylight yesterday afternoon. Each held a pistol and robbed banknotes, silver dollars, and gold jewelry worth more than 5,600 yuan.

The details are as follows:

Buying a Gold Thread Ring: Fei Wenyuan Silver Shop has been open for many years on the west side of Nanjing Road's Ball Field. At about 3:30 PM yesterday afternoon, when customers were at their peak, a man with luxurious clothes, very much like a high-class person, came outside the counter and claimed that he wanted to buy a gold thread ring. The shop assistant asked how much silver dollars he wanted, and the customer replied that one worth more than ten yuan would be fine. The shop assistant immediately approached and entered the goods room to take out several gold thread rings weighing seven or eight points to let the customer choose. Who knew that at this time, there were three more people outside the counter, each with a pistol raised in their hands. They told the crowd not to make a sound. At the same time, they jumped into the counter and divided into two groups to invade. One robber specialized in robbing the banknotes and silver dollars on the account table, while the other two robbers invaded the goods room to rob gold jewelry such as rings and earrings. There were two other robbers outside the door who were responsible for keeping watch. If anyone was spying or causing trouble, they would use a pistol to command them. Their attitude was very calm.

Innocent Disaster for Customers: When the robbers were robbing, a Cantonese customer, A, brought gold ornaments to exchange for silver dollars, weighing a total of one tael and six points. After the shop assistant calculated it, the silver dollars were valued at 102 yuan. Both the gold and silver notes were placed on the counter. The robbers took everything without hesitation, and the customer left empty-handed, extremely frustrated. The total loss was more than 1,000 yuan in banknotes, 180 gold thread rings weighing 39 taels, and 36 pairs of earrings weighing 5 taels, totaling 44 taels. Including the aforementioned banknotes and silver dollars, the total value was more than 5,600 yuan. After the robbers had robbed to their fill, they swaggered away. The responsible police station was notified and immediately sent detectives to the scene to investigate in order to arrest the murderers and recover the stolen goods.

Tragedy of a German Merchant Ship Colliding with a Mud Boat 156

German Ship Escaped After Causing the Accident

Two Girls Suffocated in the Boat

The day before yesterday at noon, 11 mud boats of the Xideji Dredging Company were fully loaded with mud from dredging machines at the Yuhang Wharf on the Bund and transported to Yangshupu to dump. After the unloading, they were still driving upstream in a continuous stream. When they reached the vicinity of the Qichang Wharf on the Bund, an imported merchant ship was turning around in the middle of the river. At the same time, a German merchant ship was sailing rapidly downstream. In order to avoid the turning merchant ship, the helmsman was not careful and suddenly violently rammed into Zhu Zhaoyou's mud boat. The boat was immediately overturned. There were six people on the boat, including Zhu and his wife, three daughters, and a boatman. They all fell into the river at the same time and were rescued by other mud boats. Zhu and his wife, their six-year-old eldest daughter, and a boatman were rescued. Zhu's four-year-old second daughter and two-year-old youngest daughter were missing. The German ship sped away after causing the accident. Zhu and others did not remember the ship's number. Afterwards, other mud boats towed Zhu's boat to the mud beach and used manpower to turn the boat over. They saw that Zhu's second and youngest daughters had both suffocated in the cabin. The situation was extremely tragic. Afterwards, Zhu personally went to the water police station to cry and complain. The head of the police station sent detective Huang Songsheng to the scene of the accident and transported the bodies of the two children to the Nanshi Lifesaving Bureau for an autopsy. The local court appointed Wang Sixian, an inspector, to examine the bodies and confirm that they had died of suffocation after the boat capsized. He ordered the father of the deceased to temporarily collect the bodies for burial. It is said that Zhu went to the police station again yesterday to demand that the ship company responsible for the accident compensate for the loss of the boat and provide generous compensation for the two daughters. The head of the police station then ordered Hua detective Wang Haiquan to investigate the ship company and the name of the ship responsible for the accident in order to negotiate and sent Zhu to the local court to investigate and pursue the matter.

Preliminary Hearing for Water Police Detective's Fatal Assault Case 157

Grandmother of Deceased Claims Dependence on Grandson for Livelihood

Equivalent to Indirectly Killing Entire Family

｜Detective Also Accused of Extorting Thousands of Dollars｜

The case of Zhang Zhaoxiang, a detective chief of the Fourth District of the Jiangsu Province Water Police Team, who assaulted boat dweller Lu A'gen, resulting in his death, was again brought before Prosecutor Yang yesterday for a preliminary hearing. The deceased's grandmother, Yang, filed a complaint, stating that her entire family relied on her grandson for their livelihood, and that this was equivalent to indirectly killing her entire family. The case not only has witness Lu Genxiang, who saw the incident, but also boatman Zhang A'dong, who personally witnessed Zhang assaulting her grandson to death for embezzling cotton. Therefore, she requests punishment for the murderer and compensation, among other things. Lu Genxiang testified that he was cooking on the boat when, on the 16th day of the lunar new year, Zhang seized the cargo. When the goods were handed over on March 28th of the Gregorian calendar, it was discovered that a significant amount was missing. Therefore, he asked Zhang to go to the Wing On Cotton Mill to provide proof. Zhang then slapped the deceased and punched him twice, resulting in his death. Zhang A'dong's testimony was similar. The official ordered them to leave and await legal punishment. However, Zhang denied the assault. The official, believing that the death was caused by injury to the ear, ordered the case to be temporarily adjourned. Subsequently, the case of merchant ship owner Guo Shixin accusing Zhang Zhaoxiang of extorting thousands of dollars was heard. Guo testified that Zhang falsely accused him of carrying contraband, seized his ship, and extorted money. This has already been proven to be a false accusation, and he requests prosecution. He also presented two witnesses, Wang Huaiquan and Cai Yiting. The official summoned the two witnesses to court for questioning. After they provided evidence, they were also instructed to leave, and both cases will be handled together.

Suspicious Powder 158

Emitting a Strange Odor When Baked

Police Confiscated Twelve Ounces

Suspected of Containing Morphine

To Be Confirmed Before Further Action

Upstairs at number 570, Dexing Lane, Peng Road, lived a Wang family. Zheng Peijin, from Yong, Jiangsu, had recently lost his job and was lodging with the Wangs. The previous morning, Wang and his wife, Li, went out and did not return until night. Zheng was alone in his room, and the other residents of the house paid him no attention. After 9:00 PM, Su Qiaoyun, a woman from Nanjing who lived downstairs, suddenly smelled a strange odor. Upon closer inspection, she realized it was coming from upstairs. She went to investigate and saw Zheng facing the stove, baking a very fine powder. She asked him what the powder was and what it was used for. Zheng said it was glutinous rice flour. The woman, suspecting he was lying, did not press him further. She took a small amount of the powder and tried to leave, but Zheng tried to stop her in every way and demanded the powder back. The woman then cried for help and seized the opportunity to escape and report to the nearby police. The police went upstairs and searched, finding a bag of fine powder weighing twelve ounces under the bed. They took Zheng into custody and brought him to the Zhabei Police Station. Yesterday, he was handed over to the Special District Local Court. After a preliminary hearing by Judge Feng, the police lawyer stated that the powder was suspected of containing morphine and requested a postponement for testing. The judge agreed to postpone the hearing until the test results were clear. Zheng testified that Wang and Li had instructed him to bake the powder, saying it could cure toothaches and fevers. He did not know what medicinal ingredients were used in the preparation. Judge Feng then ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and adjourned the hearing until the test results were clear.

Trial of Concubine Zhang Shi-ming's Lawsuit to Recognize Her Son 159

Concubine Zhang Claims to Have Endured Hardship

Requests Confirmation of Mother-Son Relationship

Arguments Concluded, Verdict on the 9th

Zhang Shi-ming, a wealthy resident of Nanxun, formerly took Zhou Miaoying as a concubine, and she bore him a son named Qu'an. When Qu'an was five years old, Miaoying was dismissed from the household. Now that Qu'an is approaching adulthood, his primary wife, Xu, married him to a niece last year. Upon learning of this, Miaoying came out to obstruct the marriage, causing Xu to secretly complete the marriage for her son. This made Miaoying even more angry, and she hired lawyers Wu Jingxiong, Yuan Yang'an, and others to file a lawsuit against Zhang Qu'an and Zhang Xu to confirm the mother-son relationship. This case was previously reported. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong of the Special Court held a hearing to question the defendants, who also hired three lawyers: Zhu Sifu, Jiang Yiping, and Cai Ni Pei. According to Zhou Miaoying's testimony, she currently resides at number 15, Yongli Lane, Tongfu Road. She was formerly married to Zhang Shi-ming as a concubine and gave birth to a son, Qu'an. She left the Zhang family when Qu'an was five years old. Now, because Zhang's wife, Xu, has surrounded my son, preventing him from knowing that his biological mother is still alive and enduring hardship outside, and preventing me from seeing my son, I am specifically suing for a judgment confirming that Qu'an is my biological son. Judge Xu asked about the record established on September 17th of the seventeenth year, separating her from the defendants. Zhou replied that the document was entirely drafted by lawyers, and she did not understand its contents. The plaintiff's lawyer then added that the precedents of the Supreme Court clearly state that the mother-son relationship can never be severed. Even if the biological mother remarries, she still has a mother-son relationship with the son born to her former husband. The defendant's lawyer, Zhu Sifu, also stated that he was present when this document was drawn up because he represented the defendant. He witnessed the plaintiff signing and sealing the document. At that time, the defendant gave the plaintiff 40,000 yuan as lifelong alimony, and the plaintiff had no property or other relationship with the defendant forever. All of this is recorded in the document, and it also declares that the plaintiff acknowledges Qu'an as his biological mother. Now, the plaintiff is again requesting confirmation of her biological mother status, which is unnecessary. Therefore, this case does not require litigation. Lawyer Cai then continued, "After the plaintiff was dismissed from the household, her whereabouts were unknown for a long time. Later, it was heard that she had joined the prostitutes at Flower Stamen Garden in Leyu Lane. She had long since severed ties with the Zhang family. What relationship is there to speak of? Only the name of mother and son remains, and there should be no further claims." Lawyer Jiang Yiping added that when the plaintiff was dismissed from the household, why didn't she request custody of her son? It is only now, when her son has the power to manage property, that she suddenly brings up this claim, which is too late. Although her request appears to be a legal issue on the surface, she actually wants to exercise maternal power, but there is no legal basis for it. Moreover, she received 40,000 yuan in lifelong alimony many years ago." Therefore, the lawyers on both sides spoke and argued until half past noon before finishing. The official then adjourned the court, announcing that the verdict would be delivered on the morning of the 9th of this month.

Conflict Arises from Quarrel with Mother-in-Law

However, Dashi, considering that his father-in-law was an elder, suppressed his anger. In extreme anger, he picked up a wooden stick next to him and struck his head violently, injuring a vital point. He immediately fell to the ground and died. The father-in-law, seeing that he had caused a disaster, immediately fled. When Dashi's parents heard about it, they will negotiate with Yang Jiusi.

Jianghai Customs Announces New Rules for Merchant Ship Hatch Manifests 177

Jianghai Customs has issued new rules for import ship manifests to strictly prevent tax evasion and has notified all shipping bureaus. The general rules are as follows: (1) All merchant ships entering Chinese territorial waters or sailing within Chinese territorial waters shall have a hatch manifest signed by the shipowner, detailing the cargo loaded, and shall be subject to customs inspection at any time. Failure to prepare this hatch manifest shall result in a fine of up to 500 taels of customs silver for the shipowner. (2) The hatch manifest shall include the ship's name, nationality, shipowner's name, and the number of pieces of cargo, as well as the numbers, marks, and packaging styles of each piece of cargo. (3) The designated port for loading and unloading goods. (4) Omitted. (5) If there are any goods (including transit goods) on board that are not listed on the hatch manifest or that do not match what is listed on the manifest, the shipowner shall request corrections from customs within 24 hours of reporting to customs, but only if the errors are due to oversight or clerical errors. However, corrections may not be requested for goods not listed on the hatch manifest that have already been discovered by customs. (6) If any goods not listed on the hatch manifest are discovered by customs officials, the shipowner and cargo owner shall each be fined up to 1,000 taels of customs silver, and the goods shall be confiscated. If the goods not listed on the manifest are hidden by special means and the customs officers confirm that the shipowner and shipowner have fulfilled their duties, paid close attention, and were unaware that private goods were hidden, the penalty may be reduced accordingly. If several packages are combined into one piece of cargo and the words "several packages combined" are not noted, it shall be treated as not listed on the hatch manifest. (7) If goods that have been listed on the hatch manifest are found by customs officials not to be among the goods carried by the ship, if the shipowner cannot provide conclusive proof that the missing goods were not loaded at the original port of departure or were mistakenly unloaded at a port along the way, the shipowner shall be fined up to 500 taels of customs silver for each missing piece of cargo. (8) If a merchant ship exports goods without customs approval, it will be fined 1,000 taels of customs silver. (9) Warships, yachts, and river patrol boats are not subject to these regulations.

Annual Meeting of the Chinese Medical Association Opens Yesterday 178

Over Five Hundred Attendees

The annual meeting of the Republic of China Medical Association, the twelfth session, began yesterday (the 3rd) at the Ningbo Native Place Association on Xizang Road. A detailed account of the opening ceremony and lectures is given below:

Attendees: Yan Zhizhong, representative of the Nanjing Ministry of Health; Cen Dezhang, representative of the Shanghai Municipal Government; Xu Shijin, representative of the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau; Kubota Harumitsu, representative of the Manchurian Medical Association; Professor Imamura Shinkichi of Tokyo Imperial University; Zeng Guangfang, director of the Natural Science Institute; Pan Ruitang, representative of the New Pharmaceutical Industry Association; Chu Minyi, representative of the National Physicians' Federation; Xu Naili, representative of the Shanghai Physicians' Association; Li Suizhi, representative of the Hangzhou Pharmaceutical Association; Huang Minglong, representative of the Chinese Pharmaceutical Association; representatives of students from Tongji, Tongde, Southeast, and Cihang medical schools; and over 500 members of the association, including Chen Fangzhi, Yu Yunxiu, Wu Yugang, Xia Shenchu, and Jiang Zhenxun.

Conference Staff: (Presidium) Chu Minyi, Chen Fangzhi, Yu Yunxiu, Hong Shilu, Lin Sumin; (Master of Ceremonies) Ye Zhisheng; (Recorders) Tang Shou Xian, Cao Zhigong; (Reception) Wang Gangang, Deng Yuanhe, Wang Fuzhong, Wang Zhangfu, Zhang Jianren, Xie Yunshou, and over ten others.

Proceedings: The opening ceremony began at 9:00 AM. After the chairman, Chen Fangzhi, performed the rituals, he gave a report stating that the association was established in the fourth year of the Republic (1915) and that sixteen years had passed. However, in recent years, due to members being scattered in various locations, it has been difficult to convene the meeting, and only today is the tenth conference being held. This is a regret of the general assembly. The association's past work has been to review and approve medical and pharmaceutical terms, etc., which has not contributed much to society. However, limited by the environment, it can only proceed gradually. In this time of disputes between old and new medicine, the association's members should uphold Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, promote the spirit of scientific nation-building, and strive constantly. This is the hope of all members, united as one. Next, Yan Zhizhong, the representative of the Ministry of Health, read a congratulatory speech (omitted). Cen Dezhang, the representative of the Municipal Government, and Xu Shijin, the representative of the Municipal Health Bureau, gave speeches of encouragement. Then, Chu Minyi, the representative of the National Physicians' Federation; Li Suizhi, the representative of the Hangzhou Pharmaceutical Association; Ivitsky, the deputy director of the Chinese Eastern Railway Health Department; Huang Minglong, the representative of the Chinese Pharmaceutical Association; and Kubota Harumitsu, the representative of the Manchurian Medical Association, read congratulatory speeches (omitted). The chairman gave a speech of thanks. After a photograph was taken, the academic lectures began. Chu Minyi and Lin Sumin took turns presiding. First, Chen Fangzhi spoke on the subject of "Research on Blood Fluke Disease (commonly known as leech tumor), First Report," detailing the origin and investigation of the disease in great detail. Next, Yu Wangda spoke on the subject of "The Compilation Process of the Chinese Pharmacopoeia." After the lecture, a break was announced. Special lectures were held from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM. Hong Shilu and Mao Xian took turns presiding. First, Professor Imamura Shinkichi from Japan gave a lecture on "Physiological Explanation of Styrism," which was translated by Sun Xiaokuan. Next, Professor Kubota Harumitsu gave a lecture on "Research on Traditional Sino-Japanese Medicine Belonging to the Menispermaceae Family," which was translated by Li Suizhi. In addition to the members of the association, many students from various medical schools attended. The meeting was adjourned at around 4:00 PM.

Registered Representatives: The number of representatives from various provincial and regional branches who registered this time was quite large. The regions included Nanjing, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Wuxi, Suzhou, Beiping, Harbin, South Manchuria, Tianjin, Guangdong, Jiaxing, Ningbo, Rugao, Gansu, Shaoxing, Anhui, Liaoning, and dozens of other places.

A Glimpse of the Exhibition: In addition to the various surgical achievements of Lin's Hospital, the exhibition also included participation and displays by various pharmaceutical companies, all of which were quite excellent. On the Chinese side, the various medical appliances of Dahua Ironworks, the various good medicines of Fukang Pharmacy and Shoumin Public Company, and the various injectable drugs of Xinya Chemical Factory were all quite noteworthy. On the foreign side, pharmaceutical companies such as Schering, Kefa, Baibu, Yingrui, Celler, Shunfa, Kaili, Baoxian, Tiande Takeda, Shionogi, and Siemens displayed the latest medicines and therapeutic equipment of many kinds and gave out various gifts to the guests, who were all very pleased. Other publications such as "Social Medical Report," "Medical and Pharmaceutical Review," and "Therapeutic Medical Report" were also distributed on site.

Today's Program: Today (the 4th), the conference will continue. Special lectures will be held from 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM, members will report their experiences from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM, and special lectures will be held from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM in the afternoon. Social News

The Diary of Marshal Foch on the European War (Continued) 202

— Translated by Gu Angruo

But before we implement this strategy, we must not forget that the active participation of our allied Russian forces on the Eastern Front has pinned down the majority of the enemy forces, enabling us to achieve the victory at the Marne. It is our responsibility to assist them to the best of our ability. This is our subsequent operational policy, regardless of the outcome. Even if we do not reach the point of victory, we can at least pin down the enemy on the Western Front, leaving them no time to transfer troops to the east. The decisive battle on the Eastern Front may become the prelude to the enemy's complete victory.

However, how the operations on the Eastern and Western Fronts should coordinate completely depends on the instructions of the French Commander-in-Chief. Unlike our offensive in the north, which was initiated by us, my current duty is to follow General Joffre's instructions and cooperate closely with the British and Belgian allied forces to direct the war...

Many of our troops left the northern war zone to recuperate in the rear or were assigned by the Commander-in-Chief. I took the opportunity to visit them. I often gathered the officers together to talk. Even after a winter of fierce fighting, the officers and soldiers were still as spirited as ever, which was highly commendable. They fully understood the importance of the battle achievements in overturning the enemy's plans at Ypres and the Yser River. They firmly believed that they would be able to defeat the enemy in their current attacks. The confidence overflowing from their faces was very moving.

On January 17th, General Zhentian was injured in a car collision, which was serious enough to cause serious consequences. We were traveling in the same car along the road from Lusibuzhi to Dankek. A heavy truck, its steering gear broken, suddenly blocked the road, and the two vehicles collided. The Commander-in-Chief was seriously injured, and he had to abandon the inspection and return to Romilly, his headquarters, by train. I was fortunate to be unharmed, but I was very worried about my superior. After leaving him at Dankek Station, this feeling was even stronger. Fortunately, he fully recovered after a few days.

After the accident, I immediately wrote to the Minister of War, as I was the assistant to the Commander-in-Chief, which was appropriate. In the letter, I asked him what I should do if General Joffre was unable to continue commanding the war as a result. If such a situation did occur, which officer on the front line would be responsible for planning emergency measures, as the enemy could take advantage of the situation at any time. The reply informed me that I did not need to worry about accidental events, as the government had already made preparations for this. In fact, in August, General Gallieni had already been internally designated as the successor to the Commander-in-Chief. Although he was extremely intelligent and talented, he had only participated in a very small part of the war, especially in trench warfare. Politicians decide too quickly about military personnel. The only place to evaluate officers is on the battlefield. Only their battle achievements are the measure of their abilities.

At the beginning of December, the British government expressed to the French government the hope of transferring the British troops in Flanders to a more northerly war zone, where they could defend part of the allied front line near the coast. Their left wing could especially rely on the sea as a support. It was thought that such a movement would satisfy British public opinion.

On the Belgian coast, from Asdun to Zeebrugge, Great Britain was often exposed to the danger of enemy attacks. Attacking Asdun's naval base with British troops along the coast would be most effective in resisting this fear. The British First Lord of the Admiralty, Mr. Churchill, attached particular importance to this plan, followed by Sir John French, the British Commander-in-Chief, and then General Joffre, the French Commander-in-Chief.

The two of them saw that the main force of the British army was devoted to goals that only concerned naval warfare, and detached from the battle against the allied forces' powerful enemy – the German army – which was quite unwise. This battle would determine the fate of the great war within three months. Under these circumstances, after lengthy discussions, it was decided in the second half of December that the British army would maintain the right wing of La Bassée while using the reinforcements arriving from their own country to transfer defenses with the French Eighth Army. The French army would leave its original troops in Nieuport, but gradually withdraw the troops from the Ypres salient, leaving only a detachment in Ypres, inserted between the British army's left wing and the Belgian army's right wing.

Later, in the implementation of this troop transfer plan, firstly, because the arrival of British reinforcements was delayed, there was a great delay. Lord Kitchener, the Secretary of State for War, was only willing to send troops to the mainland that had already been fully organized into divisions or corps. General Commander French, however, wanted them to be formed into battalions. The lack of munitions also made the Commander-in-Chief feel quite constrained in expanding the front line. The slow progress of British munitions production especially worried him.

At that time, the British First Lord of the Admiralty wanted to reconsider his plan to attack Asdun, and was willing to supply the French detachment in Nieuport with 3,000 marine reinforcements. General Joffre still insisted that land-based warfare was more important, and said that in the La Bassée area, the British forces on the left wing of our Tenth Army could be well-commanded. He therefore asked Sir John French to agree on two points: the expansion of the British army's front line and close cooperation in the French army's attacks.

The progress of the war was hindered by the lack of allied firepower and war materials. As mentioned earlier, the prolongation of the stalemate and the resulting anxiety among the people misled a certain cabinet into participating in the command of the war, making the work of the supreme military commander even more difficult. Moreover, our lack of materials had serious consequences.

Troop equipment and munitions supply have become the most important issues in modern warfare. They must occupy a prominent position in the views of the supreme military commander, not only in terms of meeting the enemy, but also in maintaining the war when public opinion or the government wavers.

As a result of this complex situation, the British army only replaced the French 16th Army Corps by the end of January, much slower than the mutually agreed progress. The French 9th and 20th Army Corps had not yet been replaced. This situation did not change significantly until mid-March. However, on that day, the British First Army completed its preparations for an attack in the La Bassée area, and the ongoing negotiations were interrupted. They could not be resumed until this plan had yielded results.

General Haig, commanding the British First Army, was ordered to attack. The troops moved forward on March 10th. At first, they had some success. In the following days, they were unable to advance, and were even unable to fully hold their ground.

On the night of March 12-13, General Haig ordered the attack to be stopped, but the occupied positions must be held firmly for ten days. The decision of the commander of the British First Army was said to be due to fears of insufficient munitions and excessive casualties.

Now we can return to the plan to replace the French army corps around Ypres. Sir John French, Lord Kitchener, General Joffre, and Mr. Millerand decided at the Chantilly Conference that the British Second Army would replace the French 9th and 20th Army Corps by April 20th. Two newly formed British divisions were transferred to France. The French army launched an offensive in Artois at the end of April, making rapid progress. On April 7th, the 9th Army Corps had withdrawn from the front line and moved to the 10th Army's war zone. On April 19th, the 20th Army Corps followed suit. By the end of April, the allied forces in the north had been completely reconfigured.

The British army deployed from the La Bassée Canal to Boesinghe on the road to Ypres. They were divided into two armies: the First Army in the south, commanded by Sir Douglas Haig, and the Second Army in the north, commanded by General Smith-Dorrien.

The French Eighth Army had disintegrated on April 4th, and was now replaced by a Belgian detachment led by General Putz. The detachment was divided into two branches, one in Ypres between the British and Belgian armies, and the other in Nieuport, the extreme left wing of the allied front line.

At my request, the Belgian army has now agreed to expand its front from Nieuport, defended by the French army, to Steneskerke. The morale of the Belgian army has been improving continuously since arriving at the Yser River. The Belgian King still holds the same determination. Although the Belgian army cannot undertake large-scale battles, they can at least lend a helping hand. They have been doing so since the beginning of March. From March 11th to April 11th, for a full month, they were ordered to fight without stopping. Although their attacks did not achieve much, they were at least able to develop a spirit of courage in the Belgian army, proving that they had the will to do their duty. Moreover, this action must have a violent reaction on the enemy's side.

We have developed close relationships with the Belgian commander and all levels of the Belgian military, which has resulted in the two armies being of one mind and one heart, which can have a very good influence in critical times.

In January, the Belgian General Headquarters withdrew from Furnes and moved to Houtem, a more remote location, because its location was often subjected to heavy enemy artillery fire. The King, Queen, and Princes resided in La Panne, a seaside town not far from Houtem. He went to the General Headquarters in the Presbyterian Church in Reninge every day. Several of his officers also lived there. (To be continued)
